< Text>
After we ordered and were handed drink cups, we went to the soda fountain to find that a couple sodas were out of order and if we wanted one of those drinks to ask for it at the counter. The lady working there looked confused when I asked her for Sprite. She said it only comes in a can and she would give it to me if I paid $1. Why should I pay more? I already bought a drink. She ended up just giving me the can for no additional charge, but she made me give her back the cup which I HOPE she does not put back and give to another customer. Despite just opening, the tables were covered in rice which means the tables were dirty all night. The food was hot and fresh. The overall taste was decent. Before leaving, I noticed that a fountain drink cost MORE than a can. Even though it was only a dollar plus change difference and I didnt want to make a huge deal out of it, the lady working at the cash register made a face and walked away as soon as I pointed it out. First visit to Flame Broiler, will most likely NEVER come to this location again.</Text>

I apologize for any inconvenience you experienced when picking up your vehicle late in the afternoon, but our parking lot can get a little busy at times. I would like to clarify some of the concerns that you stated in your review. First, I‚Äôd like to explain what was done to determine that your truck has a leaking head gasket on Cylinder #3. We initially scanned your engine computer, and it coded a P0303 indicating that the engine had a misfire in Cylinder #3 and a code P0117 indicating that your engine overheated and exceeded 286 degrees Fahrenheit. We removed the #3 spark plug and inserted a bore scope to visually inspect the cylinder. The technician observed that the cylinder was washed clean indicating that coolant was leaking into the #3 cylinder when under pressure. This was confirmed when he pressurized the cooling system and observed coolant leaking down the cylinder wall. <Review>I took my truck in to get an alignment and ride height adjustment from a local shop in Carlsbad with a computerized alignment machine after replacing the upper and lower control arms, steering center link, and tie rod ends on my 2000 Nissan Frontier.

I dropped the vehicle off at 8:30am.  Stu, the service adviser, quoted me $99.95 for the alignment and an unspecified amount for the ride height adjustment via adjusting the torsion bars in the front suspension.  They were not finished with the vehicle until 5:20pm, 20 minutes after closing.  The mechanic who worked on the vehicle informed the service adviser that I would need to "rotate the tires and tighten the ladder bars" as he was running late for a family matter and "had to go."  Stu called me at approximately 4:15pm and informed me that the final bill would be $225 for all of the work despite the technician still working on the vehicle.  An additional $125 for a ride height adjustment seemed to be a bit steep for the amount of work involved, but I was happy with their willingness to perform the final adjustments as my initial measurements indicated a ride height (ground-to-fender opening) of 28.5" (driver-side) versus 29.25" (passenger-side).  After leaving the shop, I immediately noticed that my truck was still pulling to the right...certainly better that it initially was, but not quite good enough.  I turned right around and headed back to the shop and caught Stu before he left the premises.  He reiterated that the technician suggested that I rotate the tires.  I went home and immediately did as he suggested.  The pulling was corrected to near perfect alignment with that fix.  Furthermore, the new ride height was now even as well.  However, it was now set at 32.375" which left my truck looking a little lifted in the front and not even from front-to-back.

Overall, the only criticism that I would note is that the 1-2 hours worth of work ended up taking the entire day and therefore left the technician feeling slightly rushed to get my truck pushed out at the last minute with further instructions to have me complete the rest of the required work.  I'm happy that my vehicle now drives straight, however, the extra $125 that I was charged for a ride height adjustment will likely need to be redone by either myself or another shop in order to enable a level appearance from front-to-back.

I may return to have this shop perform additional work on my vehicle in the future but might just work to get more clarity on the exact costs involved beforehand and a more accurate time frame of when they would expect to have my vehicle done...or at least arrange to schedule an appointment ahead of time to ensure that my vehicle would have the highest priority after dropping it off.</Review><Rate>4< /Rate>< Resp>

< Review>
I usually go to dealers to have important work done on my cars. However, I now have a better way to resolve automotive issues. CARLESBAD AUTO SERVICE (CAS). Our relationship started a few years ago when my son was playing hockey for San Diego and had his car here for necessary transportation. We went to the Jeep dealership. We needed tires and felt the brakes were going. They wanted a complete brake job and $700+ for tires. Wedecided to look to other options and went to CAS (they were recommended by many on Nextdoor). The owner examined the brakes and tires. They sold us a set of new tires for a bit over $500, and examined the brakes and told us the front were at 60% and the back at 50%. A far cry from the dealership. So that brings us to now. We had some brake issues (it had been two years). Took it to Jeep, $1600 for brakes ($ 120 for diagnosis).  We remembered Carlsbad and how well they had treated us three years before. We called them got a verbal estimate of a bit under $1000. We took it in and asked them to do the work. Craig and the staff up front were very friendly, cordial, and professional. It was a fun chat. Anyway, they took the keys and the car. I got a call about four hours later as they confirmed the bad brakes on the front, but said the rear brakes were still over 50% and would require minor adjustment. I have a good running and stopping auto now. This was for less than one third of what Jeep wanted. That's a big deal. A good job. Fantastic People. They're my mechanic shop now.</Review>

I read your review and would like to clarify why your Honda failed its smog check. Our technician found that your vehicle had the wrong air filter housing installed. The one your vehicle had on it when the test was performed is for a standard 1.8L engine and possibly an older version of that engine. Your Honda has an Si 2.0L V-TEC high performance engine. The State of California Smog Check Program considers this a tampered emissions failure. Your test report indicates a TAMPER failure. The State of California requires us to test the vehicle as it is when it arrives. When my husband found out I like Curry House, too, he took me there for our first date, and he proposed to me at Curry House five years later, so we decided to try and ask Curry House to be cater for our wedding even though that's not something they did, and they agreed!!

During the whole process of planning our wedding reception, I realize how humble and kind the people I worked with from Curry House are, that makes me respect this restaurant/company even more. Atsutoshi was the representative of Curry House who coordinated our wedding catering project. He was the one who spent hours planning, discussing with our wedding planner, his manager, chefs, and servers, and visited the venue many times to make sure things go smoothly on our wedding day. Although, meeting and discussing with people were his job, however, knowing that we had a limited budget, he sure made some sacrifice and was working with a diligent heart and humble attitudes, we were so pleased that we can't ask more from them. Atsu worked everything he could to meet our expectations. We weren't worried during the planning, and certainly enjoyed the food on our special day with our guests. We are just too proud to have Curry House doing the catering business for us!<//text>

<Review>Love me some great Thai food!
We were in the mood to have some coconut soup so we decided to try this place out. They have a pretty decent size parking structure that they share with other businesses so you won't have a problem parking.
However if you want to use the restroom, you have to exit the restaurant with a key that they provide and it's located outside the restaurant, corner of the plaza.
It's not the most clean place so don't expect to have 5 star treatment. When we arrived there table next to us was still dirty from the previous customers and it took them a while to clean it. Our table also had some crumbs on it as well which we asked to be cleaned again.
Right when we sat down we ordered: Devil Wings as appetizer, one big order of Tom Kha with chicken and one Pad See Ew with no meat, just veggies.
Which we waited they brought out complimentary shrimp skin which was oily but good.
Not long after our food arrived. The Devil Wings were amazing!! They came with a side of Brussels sprouts and cauliflowers around it which was incredibly delicious. The wings themselves were very juicy and meaty. So amazing. The Tom Kha was wonderful as well. The broth was very delicious and coconuty. There was a lot of chicken in there, more than it should've been. But it still gave it a nice flavor. We ended up leaving a huge chuck of chicken leftover since there was too much of it in there. Lastly, the Pan See Ew with veggies. This was also great. The noodles were perfectly cooked and the veggies were nicely steamed and they came the dish a beautiful color.
Overall the food was amazing, if you can overlook the fact that the bathroom is located outside of the restaurant and the fact that it's not super clean it's a pretty decent place to grab a quick lunch or dinner.< /Review>< Response>
None< /Response>

I returned to the dealership at 10:30am to pick up my car. Once, I arrived home and was out of my car I reached in to grab my purse and realized there was an approximate 1 to 1 1/2 inch cut on the driver seat caused at the Covina Chevrolet Dealership. I promptly drove back and was helped by the same service member. He came out to inspect the damage to my leather seat and said I would have to wait for his service director who was busy at the moment. I waited about 20 minutes for the service director Shaun Burkel. The entire interaction with Mr. Burkel, was horrible and I am still in disbelief at how such an ill mannered and unprofessional individual could be "in charge". At no point did Mr. Burkel attempt to understand or remedy the situation. The city of Covina has a problem. I'm not referring to the traffic or polluted air we breathe every day. The problem seems to be a lot more difficult to get rid of.

The problem is Covina Chevrolet.

Covina Chevrolet has become highly skilled at dispensing misery for a premium price. I was not expecting great service, but I never expected to witness such contempt for the customers they serve.

My situation with Covina Chevrolet is miserable and ongoing, but I've discovered that it is far from isolated. There are many other folks like myself who cannot even get a simple phone call.

But this is precisely their company culture. Covina Chevrolet has an 'F' rating with the Better Business Bureau and has been charged by the FTC for truly abhorrent sales practices. They had become so adept at exploiting their most vulnerable customers that they failed to notice when their behaviors had become criminal.

Misbehavior persists, until this day, because they know that many customers are unable to properly articulate their grievances. Such phenomenal managerial arrogance to ignore the basic lessons of decency from the MJL and Sage days.

You, the consumer, have many wonderful options around the San Gabriel Valley for car servicing. Whatever your automobile needs might be, Covina Chevrolet does not have the answer. By supporting their operations, you enable them to continue defrauding the San Gabriel Valley of its sanity.

The market should be cleared for those who can compete with integrity. You have the right to be treated with respect, whether or not you have the capacity to complain.< /text>

Chevy Forums (which I recommend anyone with a problem in your GM vehicle to look at) other Chevy Malibu consumer's stated similar issues with no help from the Dealer/Manufacturer. Typical wheel & deal on minor repairs but never a conclusion to the issue leaving them stuck.

For the record, I drive at least 4 hours each day from SGV to Beverly Hills. Predatory Price Gougers

Know everything about the car and deal you want before heading in here. If you don't, they will take you for every dime you have with no hesitation. Their first offer on a 22k car was $700 a month over 72 mo. They told me it was a great deal. As someone who worked in financing I knew how ridiculous the deal was and got up to walk out. They persuaded me to stay and gave me 3 more offers before offering a payment that was even on the edges of acceptability. They told me every time that it was a great deal.

On top of that, they consistently tried to avoid the negotiation on the sticker price that was already ridiculously high. It was a struggle to start that discussion before the financing discussion and it took a long time to get them to start talking.

I entered the dealer at 4:30PM and left at 12:30AM . The negotiation took that long. After having the used car for two days I noticed there were no floor mats, the tires on the front and rear were different manufacturers, and there were spots worked over with touch up paint. When I contacted the sales person he said, "As Is." They did absolutely nothing to show they were interested in the welfare of their costumers. From offering ludicrous financing to no post customer help they were horrible. I received my tags and licenses today and I was elated to take their registration sticker from my windshield.

For anyone looking to purchase a car, look elsewhere. This dealers business practices are far beyond the typical predatory nature of most car dealerships.

*They didn't smog the used vehicle and two months after purchase notified me to drive 40 mi to them from where I work and live so that they could finish the registration process. When I showed up they sent me to a local gas station instead of handling it themselves.</Review>
